<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols_and_insignia">Symbols and insignia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Symbols and insignia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Overseas_Territories_flags_(8958664223).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Overseas_Territories_flags_%288958664223%29.jpg/220px-Overseas_Territories_flags_%288958664223%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Overseas_Territories_flags_%288958664223%29.jpg/330px-Overseas_Territories_flags_%288958664223%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Overseas_Territories_flags_%288958664223%29.jpg/440px-Overseas_Territories_flags_%288958664223%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2136" data-file-height="1424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Overseas_Territories_flags_(8958664223).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Overseas Territories flags in Parliament Square in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Each overseas territory has been granted its own flag and coat of arms by the British monarch. Traditionally, the flags follow the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ensign" title="Blue Ensign">Blue Ensign</a> design, with the <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Flag_terminology" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag terminology">canton</a>, and the territory's coat of arms in the fly. Exceptions to this are Bermuda which uses a <a href="/wiki/Red_Ensign" title="Red Ensign">Red Ensign</a>; British Antarctic Territory which uses a <a href="/wiki/White_Ensign" title="White Ensign">White Ensign</a>, but without the overall cross of St. George; British Indian Ocean Territory which uses a Blue Ensign with wavy lines to symbolise the sea; and Gibraltar which uses a banner of its <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Gibraltar" title="Coat of arms of Gibraltar">coat of arms</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Gibraltar" title="Flag of Gibraltar">flag of the city of Gibraltar</a>).
</p><p>Akrotiri and Dhekelia and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena,_Ascension_and_Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha">Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha</a> are the only British overseas territories without their own flag. The <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a> is used in these territories.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> are the only British Overseas Territories with recognised <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committees</a> (NOCs); the <a href="/wiki/British_Olympic_Association" title="British Olympic Association">British Olympic Association</a> is recognised as the appropriate NOC for athletes from the other territories, and thus athletes who hold a British passport are eligible to represent Great Britain at the Olympic Games.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Shara_Proctor" title="Shara Proctor">Shara Proctor</a> from <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delano_Williams" title="Delano Williams">Delano Williams</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jenaya_Wade-Fray" title="Jenaya Wade-Fray">Jenaya Wade-Fray</a> from Bermuda<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Georgina_Cassar" title="Georgina Cassar">Georgina Cassar</a> from <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> strived to represent <a href="/wiki/Team_GB" title="Team GB">Team GB</a> at the <a href="/wiki/London_2012_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="London 2012 Olympics">London 2012 Olympics</a>. Proctor, Wade-Fray and Cassar qualified for Team GB, with Williams missing the cut, however wishing to represent the UK in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_national_football_team" title="Gibraltar national football team">Gibraltar national football team</a> was accepted into <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> in 2013 in time for the 2016 European Championships. It has been accepted by <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> and went into the 2018 FIFA World Cup qualifying, where they achieved 0 points.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><div class="noresize"><map name="ImageMap_cd517f9917cfc1c5"><area href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site:_Historic_Town_of_St_George_and_Related_Fortifications,_Bermuda" shape="rect" coords="224,158,367,217" alt="Historic Town of St George and Related Fortifications, Bermuda" title="Historic Town of St George and Related Fortifications, Bermuda" /><area href="/wiki/Gough_and_Inaccessible_Islands" shape="rect" coords="366,349,487,412" alt="Gough and Inaccessible Islands" title="Gough and Inaccessible Islands" /><area href="/wiki/Henderson_Island_(Pitcairn_Islands)" shape="rect" coords="35,305,170,341" alt="Henderson Island" title="Henderson Island" /><area href="/wiki/Gorham%27s_Cave" shape="rect" coords="267,120,408,156" alt="Gorham's Cave" title="Gorham's Cave" /></map><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/BOT_World_Heritage_Sites_Map.svg/500px-BOT_World_Heritage_Sites_Map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="500" height="511" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/BOT_World_Heritage_Sites_Map.svg/750px-BOT_World_Heritage_Sites_Map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/BOT_World_Heritage_Sites_Map.svg/1000px-BOT_World_Heritage_Sites_Map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="552" usemap="#ImageMap_cd517f9917cfc1c5" /></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BOT_World_Heritage_Sites_Map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The World Heritage Sites of the UK (Overseas Territories): The natural sites of <a href="/wiki/Gough_and_Inaccessible_Islands" title="Gough and Inaccessible Islands">Gough and Inaccessible Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henderson_Island_(Pitcairn_Islands)" title="Henderson Island (Pitcairn Islands)">Henderson Island</a> are  marked green, the cultural sites of the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site:_Historic_Town_of_St_George_and_Related_Fortifications,_Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site: Historic Town of St George and Related Fortifications, Bermuda">Historic Town of St George and Related Fortifications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kourion" title="Kourion">Kourion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gorham%27s_Cave" title="Gorham's Cave">Gorham's Cave</a> are marked red.</div></div></div>
<p>The British Overseas Territories have more biodiversity than the entire UK mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-ukotcf.org_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ukotcf.org-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> There are at least 180 <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic plant species</a> in the overseas territories as opposed to only 12 on the UK mainland.  Responsibility for protection of biodiversity and meeting obligations under international environmental conventions is shared between the UK Government and the local governments of the territories.<sup id="cite_ref-kew.org_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kew.org-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two areas, <a href="/wiki/Henderson_Island_(Pitcairn_Islands)" title="Henderson Island (Pitcairn Islands)">Henderson Island</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_Islands" title="Pitcairn Islands">Pitcairn Islands</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Gough_and_Inaccessible_Islands" title="Gough and Inaccessible Islands">Gough and Inaccessible Islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tristan_Da_Cunha" class="mw-redirect" title="Tristan Da Cunha">Tristan Da Cunha</a> are listed as <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a>, and two other territories, the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena" title="Saint Helena">Saint Helena</a> are on the United Kingdom's tentative list for future <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Gibraltar's <a href="/wiki/Gorham%27s_Cave" title="Gorham&#39;s Cave">Gorham's Cave</a> Complex is also found on the UK's tentative UNESCO World Heritage Site list.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The three regions of biodiversity hotspots situated in the British Overseas Territories are the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> Islands, the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oceanian_realm" title="Oceanian realm">Oceania ecozone</a> in the Pacific.<sup id="cite_ref-kew.org_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kew.org-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The UK created the largest continuous <a href="/wiki/Marine_protected_area" title="Marine protected area">marine protected areas</a> in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Marine_Protected_Area" title="Chagos Marine Protected Area">Chagos Marine Protected Area</a>, and announced in 2015 funding to establish a new, larger, reserve around the Pitcairn Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2016, the UK government announced the intention to create a marine protected area around <a href="/wiki/Ascension_Island" title="Ascension Island">Ascension Island</a>. The protected area would be 234,291 square kilometers, half of which would be closed to fishing.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-fco-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fco_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.gov.uk/government/policies/protecting-and-developing-the-overseas-territories">"Supporting the Overseas Territories"</a>. UK Government<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">8 November</span> 2014</span>. <q>There are 14 Overseas Territories which retain a constitutional link with the UK. .... Most of the Territories are largely self-governing, each with its own constitution and its own government, which enacts local laws. Although the relationship is rooted in four centuries of shared history, the UK government's relationship with its Territories today is a modern one, based on mutual benefits and responsibilities. The foundations of this relationship are partnership, shared values and the right of the people of each territory to choose to freely choose whether to remain a British Overseas Territory or to seek an alternative future.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Supporting+the+Overseas+Territories&amp;rft.pub=UK+Government&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.gov.uk%2Fgovernment%2Fpolicies%2Fprotecting-and-developing-the-overseas-territories&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABritish+Overseas+Territories" class="Z3988"></span><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886058088">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output <li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141006173801/http://www.consoc.org.uk/other-content/about-us/discover-the-facts/what-is-the-british-constitution/in-detail/">"What is the British Constitution: The Primary Structures of the British State"</a>. The Constitution Society. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.consoc.org.uk/other-content/about-us/discover-the-facts/what-is-the-british-constitution/in-detail/">the original</a> on 6 October 2014<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">15 November</span> 2014</span>. <q>The United Kingdom also manages a number of territories which, while mostly having their own forms of government, have the Queen as their head of state, and rely on the UK for defence and security, foreign affairs and representation at the international level. They do not form part of the UK, but have an ambiguous constitutional relationship with the UK.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=What+is+the+British+Constitution%3A+The+Primary+Structures+of+the+British+State&amp;rft.pub=The+Constitution+Society&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.consoc.org.uk%2Fother-content%2Fabout-us%2Fdiscover-the-facts%2Fwhat-is-the-british-constitution%2Fin-detail%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABritish+Overseas+Territories" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
